is evident that the threat actor owns few servers and runs Bulletproof hosting or VPS services at different timelines with different names.</p><blockquote class="pj pk pl"><p id="b6e4" class="ng nh ox ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq"><strong class="ni hh">NOTE</strong>: We are not digging deep further to reveal the real identity of the Threat Actor as it is Out of Scope of this article and our main focus is on Mint Stealer.</p></blockquote><p id="cb1c" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ng nh hg ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq"><strong class="ni hh">INFRASTRUCTURE HUNT</strong></p><p id="f82e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ng nh hg ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq">Mint Stealer does not allow to self-host a C2 (Command &amp; Control) Server as the support for C2 communication is also embedded with the stealer. This is because all the server communications (VPS, VDS, Bulletproof) are hosted within the same hosting network, hence a user does not need to migrate to another server for its C2 exchange.</p><p id="90f7" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ng nh hg ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq">It maintains 2 domains namely:-</p><blockquote class="pj pk pl"><p id="829b" those IOCs on your personal/corporate network.</p><p id="4960" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ng nh hg ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq"><strong class="ni overview, I have performed a Shallow Code Analysis for this piece:-</p><blockquote class="pj pk pl"><p id="31ca" class="ng nh ox ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq">MD5: e6e620e5cac01f73d0243dc9cf684193</p></blockquote><p id="2fa7" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ng nh hg ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq">This is a Windows Executable Malware sized at 9MB that initially appeared on <strong class="ni hh">23rd June, 2024</strong>. This malware is coded in <strong class="ni hh">Visual C++</strong>.</p><p id="2973" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ng nh hg ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq">This file is being spread with various filenames such as:-</p><pre class="oh oi oj ok ol oy oz pa bp pb fn fq"><span id="6c27" class="pc pd hg oz b bg pe pf l pg ph">vadimloader<br/>vadimloader.exe<br/>2024–06–24_e6e620e5cac01f73d0243dc9cf684193_ryuk<br/>Update.exe</span></pre><blockquote class="pj pk pl"><p id="f901" class="ng nh ox ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq">NOTE: As the filename “<strong class="ni hh">VADIM</strong>” is a Russian word for “<strong class="ni hh">Powerful Ruler</strong>” or indicates a strong masculine figure.</p></blockquote><p id="571e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ng nh hg ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq">Once dropped, it initially searches for Language Support in the registry (to exclude CIS Countries).</p><p id="e772" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ng nh hg ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq">Mint Stealer (this piece) is tasked to steal sensitive information from the victim’s computer, once it gets infected.</p><p id="5266" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ng nh hg ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq">Following are the list of Cryptocurrency Wallets which Mint Stealer targets:-</p><blockquote class="pj pk pl"><p id="eda9" class="ng nh ox ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq">Electrum-LTC<br/>Electrum<br/>ElectronCash<br/>Exodus<br/>Coinom<br/>Ethereum<br/>MultiDoge</p></blockquote><p id="a4d7" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ng nh hg ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq">Apart from this, Mint Stealer is also equipped to steal browser credentials from the victims’ machine.</p><p id="7060" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ng nh hg ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq">Upon execution, it attempts to steal<strong class="ni hh"> PuTTY </strong>and <strong class="ni hh">WinSCP</strong> information including sessions, passwords etc.</p><p id="7a16" class="pw-post-body-paragraph ng nh hg ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np ni b nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od gz fq">Both domains offers Files Hosting Service and it can be assumed that the stealer or Threat Actor might have used these
